  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e5713eb0-b1d0-41e7-bd6b-66078e092382'
      });

  <span id="freeText8053743598175163304" style="display:none"><b>There’s something about the new guy at Crossroads High…</b><br /><br /><i>Most</i> sixteen-year-olds have friends. Aden Stone has four human souls living inside him:<br /><br />One can time travel.<br />One can raise the dead.<br />One can possess another human.<br />One can tell the future.<br /><br />Everyone thinks he’s crazy, which is why he’s spent his entire life shuffled between mental institutions and juvie. All of that is about to change, however. For months Aden has been having visions of a beautiful girl—a girl who carries centuries-old secrets. A girl who will either save him or destroy him.<br /><br />Together they’ll enter a dark world of intrigue and danger... but not everyone will come out alive.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_63938216" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63938216" />
    <a title="Steph Su" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2010935-steph-su"><img alt="Steph Su" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504243050p2/2010935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63938216?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Su" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Su" href="/user/show/2010935-steph-su">Steph Su</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=stick-to-writing-adult-books">stick-to-writing-adult-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63938216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6278434184192734268">It’s unfortunate that the premise is so appealing, because, for me, INTERTWINED was an overwritten, confusing, and crowded paranormal mess. Too much was implied and told directly to readers, the characters were unappealing, and the whole thing was just way too long to hold my attention.<br/><br/>Showalter has the unfortunate penchant of telling, not showing, and making her characters take agonizingly slow paragraphs to undergo a simple thinking process. Any story that relies heavily on the main characters</span>
  <span id="freeText6278434184192734268" style="display:none">It’s unfortunate that the premise is so appealing, because, for me, INTERTWINED was an overwritten, confusing, and crowded paranormal mess. Too much was implied and told directly to readers, the characters were unappealing, and the whole thing was just way too long to hold my attention.<br /><br />Showalter has the unfortunate penchant of telling, not showing, and making her characters take agonizingly slow paragraphs to undergo a simple thinking process. Any story that relies heavily on the main characters’ romantic appeal must work on showing us readers the attraction and potential, instead of telling us over and over again, “X couldn’t resist Y. Z was scared to show her feelings” etc.<br /><br />As a staunch fan of Showalter’s adult Harlequin romances, I was disappointed that she seemed to feel the need to “dumb down” her writing for the young adult crowd. Please. It’s the R-rated sexual thoughts and scenes that need to go, not intelligent character development. Teenagers can tell the difference between an author who knows the teen voice and an author who typically writes for adults and is just trying to make his or her way into the YA genre.<br /><br />It goes without saying, then, that I couldn’t make myself care for the characters. They were self-absorbed, overbearingly introverted when it came to pondering, and didn’t do anything really worth mentioning. So Aden attacks a werewolf, gets bullied, and wants to lavish the vampire princess. So Mary Ann has a few conversations with her friend and boyfriend, and continues to hang out with the werewolf even though his monstrous presence supposedly frightens her because she never knows what’s going on.<br /><br />By this point, a discerning reader will simply ask the important question: so what? Where are all of these disconnected and emotionally distant events leading up to? In the end it didn’t matter, because I was already tired of being narrated to like I have an IQ of 50 by a bunch of unlikable characters. I put the book down.<br /><br />I have to give Gena and Harlequin TEEN this, though: they certainly have the right idea of what story elements will appeal to today’s Twilight audience. Readers looking for equally emotionally tortured paranormal romances will no doubt find their way to this new line. I have not read Showalter’s other YA books, but unfortunately I just cannot tolerate stories that insult my intelligence—and nor should I have to. Next time, Gena. Next time, Harlequin TEEN.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6278434184192734268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1408876180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1408876180" />
    <a title="Naomi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20128361-naomi"><img alt="Naomi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418567627p2/20128361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1408876180?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naomi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naomi" href="/user/show/20128361-naomi">Naomi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=all-kinds-of-shapeshifters">all-kinds-of-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=gena-showalter">gena-showalter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=dragons-fairies-and-all-that">dragons-fairies-and-all-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=big-bad-vampires">big-bad-vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=big-bad-werewolves">big-bad-werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20128361-naomi?shelf=zombies-demons-angels-and-such">zombies-demons-angels-and-such</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1408876180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14159488435874371684">I haven't been able to fully read a book in weeks, I was in a big reading slump and I needed it to stop. So, I tried the only thing I thought would help me out of it, I read a book by Gena Freaking Showalter. And guess what? IT WORKED! <br/><br/>God, I love that feeling. I could not stop reading this book, I was hooked from page 1 and even Gena tried to stop me from reading INTERTWINED because she told me that this particular series has no end and I know I will be sad and mad when I actually finish it but</span>
  <span id="freeText14159488435874371684" style="display:none">I haven't been able to fully read a book in weeks, I was in a big reading slump and I needed it to stop. So, I tried the only thing I thought would help me out of it, I read a book by Gena Freaking Showalter. And guess what? IT WORKED! <br /><br />God, I love that feeling. I could not stop reading this book, I was hooked from page 1 and even Gena tried to stop me from reading INTERTWINED because she told me that this particular series has no end and I know I will be sad and mad when I actually finish it but, for now, I'm just going to enjoy the ride. And what a ride it was. Phenomenal.<br /><br />INTERTWINED is like nothing I've ever read. It's so unique and cool, I loved everything about it. Gena once again blew my mind, she's the best. I don't read a lot of YAs but, like the WHITE RABBIT CHRONICLES, I know this series will be a favorite of mine. <br /><br />This is the story of Aden, a not so normal teenager. He's not alone in his head, that sounds bad but it actually isn't. He has 4 souls trapped inside his head: Eve, Caleb, Julian and Elijah. Aden would be a normal human if not for them, they all have special powers, Eve can travel through time, Julian can raise the dead, Caleb can posses other bodies, and Elijah can predict the future. Aden lives in foster homes and he's moved into a ranch, living with other teens. In this new town he meets Mary Ann, a girl who negates his powers. When he's around her, the voices inside his head disappear and they both feel a connection toward each other, a brother/sister kind of love. Aden knows he's supposed to meet his girlfriend soon because Elijah predicted it and he does, a girl named Veronica and her protector, Riley, arrive into town not long after him. <br /><br />I can't tell you much more because I'll reveal too much and it'd just spoil the entire book for you. Trust me, you want to read this amazing book and experience it spoiler-free for the first time. All I can tell you is that there's no love triangle, if you're a love triangle hater like me, I'd like to tell you: fear not friend, Gena doesn't do love triangles, you're free to enjoy this book as much as I did. So, go buy it!<br /><br />There is so much to say about INTERTWINED. Like I said, this book is so different from what I'm used to read, even from Gena. It is Aden's story yes, but it's also Mary Ann's. We get Aden's POV but Mary Ann's as well and I loved that! Basically there are two love stories: Aden and Victoria and Mary Ann and Riley. It was just so well written, I read this book in one day and I want more. <br /><br />I loved Aden from the start, he's so lost at the beginning, he has no friends, he thinks he's weird having souls within him. But he's still strong and I loved his relationship with the 4 souls. Despite them being annoying and him wanting some peace and quiet sometimes, Aden still cares deeply about them and them about him. I found myself caring about them as well and I cried guys. I cried, I won't tell you why, but I cried! I loved watching Aden growing, his character really changed in the book, in a good way. He matured a lot, became stronger and it was a great thing to see.<br /><br />Now, Victoria. I liked her but I didn't really connect with her. She's a nice girl who truly cares about Aden but she wasn't my favorite character. I just didn't connect with her at all.<br /><br />My favorite is definitely Mary Ann though. I loved reading her POV, she's the most normal of them all but she's amazing, such a great friend, a strong girl who has her entire life turned upside down in one day. I fell in love with her and especially Riley...oh my god, RILEY! You see Cole or even Frosty from the WHITE RABBIT CHRONICLES? Well, you have Riley. <u>Pure bad boy à la Showalter.</u> And guys, he's not human, he's something else and I loved him so much! Him and Mary Ann were so cute together, I can't wait to have more of them.<blockquote>
  <b>"They entered the classroom together. Mary Ann took her seat in the far right row, closest to the teacher's desk. Kyle Matthews had the one next to her and he was already seated. As Riley had done in their first two classes, he stood in front of his desired spot and stared. Stared until Kyle was shifting uncomfortably. Stared until Kyle picked up his books and founds another seat."</b>
</blockquote>That right there is who Riley is and why I fell in love with him and why you will too.<br /><br />And for those of you who're wondering about the kissing. Once again, fear not because Gena doesn't disappoints. She loves the kissing part as much as we do.<br /><br />The story in INTERTWINED is great, a bit complicated to explain in a review and I don't want to write any spoilers so you'll have to read the book to understand but it's amazing. Gena wrote such an unique, kickass, interesting and fun book, I can't believe I haven't read it before now. The story will pull you in and you won't want to get out. <br /><br />If I had to say one little negative thing it would be that the ending was a bit abrupt and rushed. I was expecting a big fight and maybe a big cliffhanger but none of that, it was good and a satisfying ending but a bit easy for me. Still, I cannot wait to read the next book and the next one after that, and then cry because there won't be a fourth book. I'll just have to go and threaten Gena or her dogs until she writes it. That sounds like a plan!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14159488435874371684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70174898" />
    <a title="kari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2207055-kari"><img alt="kari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262446392p2/2207055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70174898?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kari" href="/user/show/2207055-kari">kari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2207055-kari?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70174898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13010966887023952521">I enjoyed this book and have only one real complaint. When a book is the start of a new series, it would be nice to know that going in, maybe put a line on the cover, first book in the exciting new series, etc. <br/>That being said and a little disappointed that I have to wait until the next book to find out what happens next, I found this book a fun read with lots, and I mean lots, of surprises.<br/>This book has a little something for everyone. There are humans, well, sort of, since they have special ab</span>
  <span id="freeText13010966887023952521" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book and have only one real complaint. When a book is the start of a new series, it would be nice to know that going in, maybe put a line on the cover, first book in the exciting new series, etc. <br />That being said and a little disappointed that I have to wait until the next book to find out what happens next, I found this book a fun read with lots, and I mean lots, of surprises.<br />This book has a little something for everyone. There are humans, well, sort of, since they have special abilities, vampires, werewolves, witches, goblins, fairies, undead, demons, ghosts, and maybe others as well. It keeps you guessing all the time of what will happen next. I couldn't put it down once I got into it.<br />Aden is a great character, from the moment you meet him, you hope that his life will get better. He deals with what he's been given as well as he can. His ability and Mary Ann's were intriguing and something new I haven't read about before. I'm looking forward to the next book exploring their relationship to one another more. What else can Mary Ann do? Or Aden?<br />It did take me a bit to get used to all the voices Aden hears, but after the first few chapters, I knew who they were and could identify who was talking, etc. <br />I'd recommend this for anyone who enjoy a fast-paced, action packed story.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_66394749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66394749" />
    <a title="Steph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2601167-steph"><img alt="Steph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337148041p2/2601167.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66394749?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph" href="/user/show/2601167-steph">Steph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66394749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8425628671413747799">I loved the concept of a character with four human souls living inside his head immediately. And when the book opened on him in a graveyard, accidentally raising the dead and then being forced to decapitate them, I was even more excited.<br/><br/>I was very disappointed to find Aden didn’t fight any more zombies through the book, but I felt the use of his other abilities incredibly interesting.<br/><br/>Many people enjoy reading paranormal romance. I can handle it, but vampires and werewolves make me cringe straigh</span>
  <span id="freeText8425628671413747799" style="display:none">I loved the concept of a character with four human souls living inside his head immediately. And when the book opened on him in a graveyard, accidentally raising the dead and then being forced to decapitate them, I was even more excited.<br /><br />I was very disappointed to find Aden didn’t fight any more zombies through the book, but I felt the use of his other abilities incredibly interesting.<br /><br />Many people enjoy reading paranormal romance. I can handle it, but vampires and werewolves make me cringe straight away. I felt in this book, the four people inside Aden’s head, with their assorted abilities of time travel, seeing the future, raising the dead and possessing others, would have had enough interesting adventures on their own, and the introduction of the vampire and werewolf love interests was done only to pull readers of Twilight. When fairies, goblins and witches started to make appearances, I was a bit unsure where it would go.<br /><br />In spite of this, I really enjoyed Intertwined. I liked the friendship between Mary Ann and Aden, as well as Aden’s relationships with the people inside his head. I like flawed protagonists in novels, and I felt Aden was, though Mary Ann was a bit of a Mary Sue. Invented details about vampires (like the fact that you can only hurt them in their eyes and ears) felt a bit unnecessary, and some of the fight scenes a bit prolonged.<br /><br />There were a couple of things I didn’t like: The vampires all had typical vampire names (Victoria, Dmitri), and Aden and Riley always felt the need to protect Mary-Ann and Victoria, and constantly assert their manliness by threatening each other (Do teenage girls find this attractive or something? I don’t get it). <br /><br />Those things aside, I felt this novel was well-executed. Though I went “What?” when more mythical creatures started to appear, my interest didn’t dwindle, the story was gripping. This will inevitably appeal to readers of paranormal romance, and if that’s you, it’s well worth checking out. I think if I were more of a fan of that genre, I would have enjoyed Intertwined a lot more. It’s already far better than Twilight for me, and really action-packed. Based on Intertwined, I’m definitely going to check out Gena Showalter’s previous YA novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8425628671413747799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText17899079201194313509" style="display:none">Quick review<br /><br /><b>Cover:</b> I like it<br /><b> Rating </b> PG-13<br /><b> Thumbs Up </b> 4<br /><b>Overall:</b> There is a lot going on.<br /><b>Characters:</b> There is a lot of them.<br /><b>Plot:</b> Dull at first but it picks up.<br /><b>Page Turner:</b> Yes, I guess<br /><b> Series Cont.?</b> Yes<br /><b> Recommend </b> Maybe<br /><b>Book Boyfriend:</b> Riley<br /><br /><b>SUMMARY</b> (50 word or less)<br /><br />Got this as a part of an audiable.com sale. <div id="review_1638096608" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1638096608" />
    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638096608?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638096608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13059671712161292434">I was about halfway through this and although I was enjoying it, I wasn't sure it was enough to continue with the rest of the series. That completely changed during the second half! I was suddenly drawn in and couldn't stop turning the pages. Vampires, werewolves, faeries, goblins and souls trapped in a human boys body? HELL YES, sign me up! The second half of the book was absolutely spellbinding and action packed and has left me itching to get my hands on the rest of this series! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer265063507158083709">Ugh. What happens when you mix Fruity Pebbles, Lucky Charms, and Cookie Crisp? You guessed it, blah.<br/>Each of them alone is awesome and delicious, but when you mix all of these elements together you get a bowl of cereal that's very difficult to keep down. <br/><br/>That's my problem with this book. It had just WAY too much going on. The whole book managed to mix Vampires/Werewolves/Vlad The Impaler/Faeries/Teenage Pregnancy/Mental Health/Abandonment/Peer Pressure/Poor parenting/Time Travel/Possession and Pr</span>
  <span id="freeText265063507158083709" style="display:none">Ugh. What happens when you mix Fruity Pebbles, Lucky Charms, and Cookie Crisp? You guessed it, blah.<br />Each of them alone is awesome and delicious, but when you mix all of these elements together you get a bowl of cereal that's very difficult to keep down. <br /><br />That's my problem with this book. It had just WAY too much going on. The whole book managed to mix Vampires/Werewolves/Vlad The Impaler/Faeries/Teenage Pregnancy/Mental Health/Abandonment/Peer Pressure/Poor parenting/Time Travel/Possession and Premonitions into a 440 page book. Sorry, it failed. Along with that, there were so many side characters, both corporeal and non, that I lost interest as soon as the vampire was introduced, which is 1/3 of the way into the book. Note to the author, this book is like a pretty girl with way too much make-up on. Strip a few of the layers, and you may have a credible base.</span>

  <span id="freeText1439840727391776613" style="display:none">I think I should receive an award for reading this book, sorry Torie, but it truly was a horrid experience, every time I picked it up, I would get a headache and fell nausea.<br /><br />This book was never on my radar.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_70886413" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70886413" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70886413?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70886413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18082184574874744385">"Intertwined" is about Aden Stone, a sixteen year old guy who goes to Crossroads High. At first he seems normal, with his smoldering looks and all, but in reality he has four voices inside of his head that each posess a supernatural power. He doesn't know where they came from or who they are; they have been with him since birth - they were always just there. Julian can raise the dead. Eve can transport Aden back to the past. Elijah can tell the future. And Caleb can posess other humans. This see</span>
  <span id="freeText18082184574874744385" style="display:none">"Intertwined" is about Aden Stone, a sixteen year old guy who goes to Crossroads High. At first he seems normal, with his smoldering looks and all, but in reality he has four voices inside of his head that each posess a supernatural power. He doesn't know where they came from or who they are; they have been with him since birth - they were always just there. Julian can raise the dead. Eve can transport Aden back to the past. Elijah can tell the future. And Caleb can posess other humans. This seems like a lot to handle in just one book, but it only gets weirder. Aden meets a girl named Mary Ann who seems to neutralize his power. He also meets a vampire princess and her wolf guardian. Not to mention the goblins, witches, and fairies he encounters. And yes all of these things are in just this book, they are in fact... intertwined. Hah! See what I did there?<br /><br />Uh yeah. Okay, anyway... I started out really liking this book. The plotline with Aden and his four mysterious souls inside his head was very intriguing. However, after he and Mary Ann meet their supposed soul mates (a vampire and a werewolf), things seem to spin out of control. There were a TON of added plot elements and storylines that could've been fleshed out more and developed - but sadly the author just attempted to add a plethora of supernatural elements to the book. This could've been a meshed up version of Twilight, some Faerie book, and a werewolf mystery.<br /><br />However, I enjoyed the story as a whole. This book kept me flipping the pages even when I had twenty text notes, an algebra test, and a biology quiz the following day. I hope if the author makes a sequel she'll try to flesh out a single plot line instead of creating a spiral of loosely related events. And also the conversation between the characters was stilted (more so towards the end of the book). A lot of YA authors seem to have this teenager conversation problem thing going on, so I didn't mind it too much though. Good effort, I think this one will become pretty popular in the future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18082184574874744385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1178606673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1178606673" />
    <a title="Sarah " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24314165-sarah"><img alt="Sarah " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453146999p2/24314165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1178606673?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah " href="/user/show/24314165-sarah">Sarah </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24314165-sarah?shelf=source-public-library">source-public-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1178606673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10652756988439234581">Dear Readers,<br/><br/>Have you ever read a book that you were so wrapped up in, so completely involved with, that by the time you finished it you had no idea what the heck your feelings are? If you have, than you can understand how I’m feeling about <em>Intertwined</em>. It’s been three days since I read this book, but I still have no freaking idea how I’m going to put this review in words you are going to understand, because I’m still thinking, “WTF did I just read?” Regardless, I’m going to try. I should be abl</span>
  <span id="freeText10652756988439234581" style="display:none">Dear Readers,<br /><br />Have you ever read a book that you were so wrapped up in, so completely involved with, that by the time you finished it you had no idea what the heck your feelings are? If you have, than you can understand how I’m feeling about <em>Intertwined</em>. It’s been three days since I read this book, but I still have no freaking idea how I’m going to put this review in words you are going to understand, because I’m still thinking, “WTF did I just read?” Regardless, I’m going to try. I should be able to make something out for you guys . . . I did write over seven pages worth of notes on the subject. *deep breath*<br /><br /><em>Intertwined </em>isn’t your average teen romance novel. For one, the main characters don’t fall in love and live happily ever after . . . with each other, anyways.<br /><blockquote><em>Were my waffles sprinkled with crack?</em>she wondered. This couldn't be real.</blockquote><br />When Aden Stone first meets Mary Ann Gray (in a desecrated graveyard after Aden accidentally causes the dead to rise . . . whoops), the heavens move, all the town’s power flickers, and they accidentally call dangerous supernatural beings from all over the world to their small town to kill investigate the source of so much power. But don’t be confusing that mutual feeling of magnetism and repulsion with love, because they don’t like each other like that. Because that would be <em>too </em>easy. No, Aden and Mary both confess they feel like long-lost siblings, but <em>why?</em><br /><br />Meanwhile, Mary is being stalked by a big, beautiful wolf with green eyes (because that’s a normal body part to be noticing when a person thinks they are minutes away from becoming a scary wolf’s next meal.) that is much too tame and non-aggressive to be an average wolf with green eyes that can somehow talk to her with his mind. At the same time, Aden has finally met the girl of his dreams that Elijah, the prophet that lives in his head, prophesied he’d meet soon before he’s killed.<br /><br />Oh, did I forget to mention he has souls taking up space in his head? Yeah, he does. No, he’s not crazy, they really live up there. Your doctors would think you have schizophrenia too if the only friends you’ve ever had live inside your brain. Let me introduce them: Elijah, the soul that can and will predict when you die. He’s never wrong, no matter what. Caleb's ability forces Aden to body hop (ironic that he can’t seem to leave Aden’s though), Julian raises the dead, which can be damn inconvenient when Aden accidentally walks into a graveyard. Then there’s Eve, the female soul stuck in Aden’s body. She’s the mother figure (can you imagine having a mother-like soul taking up real estate in your body? Yikes!) and can to take Aden into the past – <em>his past.</em><br /><br /><blockquote>❥ ❥ ❥</blockquote><br /><br /><em>[This isn’t even half of what goes down in Intertwined and I’ve already written a whole review. I haven’t even told you my opinion, yet! So if you more details, get your hands on a copy, because I have to finish this review up sometime today.]</em><br /><br />I know you can hear a lot of sarcasm in what I’ve wrote sorry not sorry but, as you can see, it gets a little ridiculous . . . and it doesn’t stop there. And yet, I had such a fun time reading this! Sure there was a few things I didn’t like about the book.<br /><br />For one, Aden and Victoria’s (Victoria is the vampire princess he falls in love with) relationship didn’t click as a good match. They’re all insta-love and no real substance, but I can’t tell if it’s deliberate because of Aden’s up-coming expiration date. I’m hoping book two gives me a clue.<br /><br />In comparison, Mary Ann and Riley’s (remember that green-eyed wolf? Yeah, he’s a werewolf. Figures) relationship is moving at a slower, more believe-able pace with much more essence. They feel like best friends turned lovers, which I absolutely enjoy. Maybe I have such a big crush on them because Riley reminds me of a big, love-able puppy. I mean, he totally loves to have his each scratched. It’s so cute. ♥_♥<br /><br />Nothing I say about this book will touch on how crazy complex this story is for young adult fiction – or any fiction, really. What is it with Showalter and her ability to take a crazy busy plot line and reel me like a small fish on a hook? I don’t stand a chance with this lady! When she throws one plot twist after another on me, she guarantees I’ll by another book. This woman is either <strong>crazy talented or just extremely sadistic</strong>. I can’t tell, all I know is I’m picking up the next book as soon as possible.<br /><p>Manipulated and loving it,<br /></p><p>✌One Curvy Blogger<br /></p><p>
  Do you like crazy busy plots or simple and sweet?
  <a href="http://onecurvyblogger.com/2015/02/02/intertwined-gena-showalter/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally posted on One Curvy Blogger</a>
</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="10652756988439234581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_50642508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50642508" />
    <a title="Lisa (A Life Bound By Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2001477-lisa-a-life-bound-by-books"><img alt="Lisa (A Life Bound By Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318132511p2/2001477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/50642508?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa (A Life Bound By Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa (A Life Bound By Books)" href="/user/show/2001477-lisa-a-life-bound-by-books">Lisa (A Life Bound By Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2001477-lisa-a-life-bound-by-books?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50642508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10680536775428759198">There’s something about the new guy at Crossroads High . . . <br/><br/>Most sixteen-year-olds have friends. Aden Stone has four human souls living inside him: <br/><br/>One can time-travel.<br/><br/>One can raise the dead.<br/><br/>One can tell the future.<br/><br/>And one can possess another human.<br/><br/>With no other family and a life spent in and out of institutions, Aden and the souls have become friends. But now they're causing him all kinds of trouble. Like, he'll blink and suddenly he's a younger Aden, reliving the past. One wrong move, and he'</span>
  <span id="freeText10680536775428759198" style="display:none">There’s something about the new guy at Crossroads High . . . <br /><br />Most sixteen-year-olds have friends. Aden Stone has four human souls living inside him: <br /><br />One can time-travel.<br /><br />One can raise the dead.<br /><br />One can tell the future.<br /><br />And one can possess another human.<br /><br />With no other family and a life spent in and out of institutions, Aden and the souls have become friends. But now they're causing him all kinds of trouble. Like, he'll blink and suddenly he's a younger Aden, reliving the past. One wrong move, and he'll change the future. Or he'll walk past a total stranger and know how and when she's going to die. He's so over it. All he wants is peace. And then he meets a girl who quiets the voices. Well, as long as he's near her. Why? Mary Ann Gray is his total opposite. <br /><br />He's a loner; she has friends. He doesn't care what anyone thinks; she tries to make everyone happy. And while he attracts the paranormal, she repels it. For her sake, he should stay away. But it's too late....<br />Somehow, they share an inexplicable bond of friendship. A bond about to be tested by a werewolf shape-shifter who wants Mary Ann for his own, and a vampire princess Aden can't resist. Two romances, both forbidden. Still, the four will enter a dark underworld of intrigue and danger but not everyone will come out alive....<br /><br />REVIEW: Somewhat confusing, with the many different story arc's but still a good read once you wade through the layers of the main and subplots of the book. Sadly, all the layers seem to only take away the ease of reading and relating to the main characters - let alone the four souls trapped in Adens head. It just makes it all little hard to follow with so much going on and so many mythical creatures popping up in what felt like every turn of the page. <br /><br />The biggest let down for me by far, was that the story was sold to me on the fact that the it was about a person with 4 souls trapped inside of him and that each one had a different ability. Seeing the future, Possessing another, Waking the Dead and Time Travel - which was amazing to read when it finally happened throughout the book. I just wished there were more interaction with the trapped souls. In my eyes with the <br />whole mix of the many different things going on in this world that Gena Showalter has written, the main plot as I saw it (the four souls) had somewhat fallen to the wayside. In the end things were tied up with the souls a little bit to quickly for what I was expecting and left me with questions that I will only hope to see the answers for in the books to follow. <br /><br />As a whole it was far from bad, just a little jumbled and confusing. Those few flaws wouldn't and won't prevent me from purchasing the next in the series as I look forward to learning more in the future and to find out just where the author will take us and her characters next.<br /><br />For more info and reviews please visit my Book Review Blog here - <a href="http://alifeboundbybooks.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">A Life Bound By Books</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10680536775428759198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_129216113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyndsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyndsey" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey">Lyndsey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=genre-urban-fantasy">genre-urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129216113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1263580425098582968">Aden has four souls living inside his body, not to mention his own. Sound confusing? Well, it is. But also strangely engaging.<br/><br/>There is so much going on in this book. Within the first couple chapters there was foreshadowing, red herrings, background stories, and multiple subplots. If your looking for something quick or easy, this isn't the one. It is definitely not a skimmer.<br/><br/>Towards the end, it became a bit of a supernatural orgy fest with ghosts, goblins, zombies, witches, psychics, empaths, wer</span>
  <span id="freeText1263580425098582968" style="display:none">Aden has four souls living inside his body, not to mention his own. Sound confusing? Well, it is. But also strangely engaging.<br /><br />There is so much going on in this book. Within the first couple chapters there was foreshadowing, red herrings, background stories, and multiple subplots. If your looking for something quick or easy, this isn't the one. It is definitely not a skimmer.<br /><br />Towards the end, it became a bit of a supernatural orgy fest with ghosts, goblins, zombies, witches, psychics, empaths, werewolves, vampires and demons (or rather half human/demon hybrids and their even more complicated spawn). Shall I go on? Because I could probably think of more. Oh yeah, time traveler!<br /><br />As much as reading that list makes me think "awesome!", it also sometimes causes an involuntary "wait, what??".<br /><br />The world building is decent. It offers a new version of vampires (Really? There are more versions?), but not a lot else is new. Warring factions of supernatural beings who all suffer from megalomania and want to rule the world. Why cant the pretty monsters all just get along? It seems like no matter what, they are always hating and fighting each other. Is it too much to ask for something different? This isn't a gripe about this book in particular, just the massive amounts of fantasy novels that seem to rely on the same formula. There's just too much of the same.<br /><br />I prefer updates of classic mythos, and some would probably say this falls into that category. But the supernatural part of the story just felt like "Okay, I've heard it all before". Maybe because i actually watch too much of CW's Supernatural, but who can say?<br /><br />The thing that most impressed me was the main concept. Five souls inhabiting one body. When I first read that, I thought that there was no way an author could pull that off. But she certainly did! The characters really all seemed unique and mostly genuine. It became fairly easy to separate them from each other, and I could almost picture what I think they all would look like if they looked like anything or anyone. What do they look like to Aden, I wonder? Maybe glowing balls of light inside his mind? I wonder if he even has an idea of what they are supposed to look like.<br /><br />As it went on though, I started to care less and less about what happened. I still liked the characters but I just felt like the story got way to complicated and too far out there. It needed to just get on with the main storyline about Aden.<br /><br />I am excited about the sequel, I just really hope that she focuses more on the main plot about the souls and less on the war of attractive beasts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1263580425098582968" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_86183016" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86183016" />
    <a title="BlueSky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3006876-bluesky"><img alt="BlueSky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262136293p2/3006876.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86183016?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BlueSky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BlueSky" href="/user/show/3006876-bluesky">BlueSky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86183016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15977991620334145052">Gena Showalter has come up with a cracker of an idea - a reform school boy, Aden, with special powers who also happens to house four other souls in his head/body (which he must keep secret or risk mental institution). Throw in a cute girl-next-door type, a vampire princess, a werewolf and a few maggot ridden zombies and she has a sure-fire formula winner. Right? Well you would think, wouldn't you? I sure got my hopes up. <br/><br/>It took until Chapter 8 (P 133) for things to start to come together. Befor</span>
  <span id="freeText15977991620334145052" style="display:none">Gena Showalter has come up with a cracker of an idea - a reform school boy, Aden, with special powers who also happens to house four other souls in his head/body (which he must keep secret or risk mental institution). Throw in a cute girl-next-door type, a vampire princess, a werewolf and a few maggot ridden zombies and she has a sure-fire formula winner. Right? Well you would think, wouldn't you? I sure got my hopes up. <br /><br />It took until Chapter 8 (P 133) for things to start to come together. Before that I had trouble keeping awake while I read. Then Chapter 13 (P 234) for the story to get really interesting - after so many pages of obvious 'fill' we finally start to get a few answers as to why our little group of 'abnormals' has been drawn together. <br /><br />Some of the characters just didn't work for me. Mary Ann was far too sweet and unassuming for a 16 year old girl. Her whole life was devoted to making others happy. As a main character she was pasty and spineless. Her relationship with her best-friend-since-toddlerhood, Penny, didn't gel. It was all fake and no substance. A lot of the secondary characters were basically stick-figures, which is OK if they don't pop up too often but not OK if they are in almost every chapter. They need connecting to the main characters with history/emotion and thereby connecting to the reader.<br /><br />And therein lies a lot of Intertwined's problem - lots of Tell going on by the author and precious little Show. There were whole chapters that were like that - sketchy and boring, jumping willy nilly from one theme to the next. Then every now and then Gena would throw in some meat but she would give too much detail! There was no balance. Sometimes it was as if another person had commenced writing a passage. She does not shine at writing her character's emotions with empathy.<br /><br />There was insufficient explanation given to certain events in the book - especially action scenes - where I suspect the author ran out of ideas so she just stopped. A bit like having a house with important rooms unfinished.<br /><br />Much was made of Aden's special abilities - but we never actually found out what they were. His four housemates seemed to be the only ones with the bags of tricks.<br /><br />I gave up by page 402. I really didn't want to know any more because it just got too silly with so many themes/ideas bubbling over. PAINFUL.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15977991620334145052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_56320669" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56320669" />
    <a title="Katie(babs)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs"><img alt="Katie(babs)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242522005p2/179852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56320669?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie(babs)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie(babs)" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs">Katie(babs)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56320669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer115355128802575487">I had very high hopes for this first YA book by Gena. I have enjoyed almost every single book Gena has written from her contemporaries, paranormals and sci-fi romances. The main storyteller is Aden Stone, an orphan in foster care who has four souls living in side of him. They each have their own paranormal abilities. Aden doesn’t know why he has these voices, but he is able to live with them. I on the other hand would be sitting in a corner, rocking screaming for them to leave me alone. Aden wou</span>
  <span id="freeText115355128802575487" style="display:none">I had very high hopes for this first YA book by Gena. I have enjoyed almost every single book Gena has written from her contemporaries, paranormals and sci-fi romances. The main storyteller is Aden Stone, an orphan in foster care who has four souls living in side of him. They each have their own paranormal abilities. Aden doesn’t know why he has these voices, but he is able to live with them. I on the other hand would be sitting in a corner, rocking screaming for them to leave me alone. Aden wouldn’t mind every once in a while if they took a rest. When Aden meets Mary Ann Gray his voices disappear. This is the first time it has ever happened to him. What is it about Mary Ann that makes her so special?<br /><br />Mary Ann finds Aden to be strange but is intrigued by him. She doesn’t think there is anything special about her. She gets good grades, goes to work and has a five-year plan set for herself. But now that Aden is going to her school, the strangest things begin to happen. A werewolf comes out of nowhere and begins to stalk her. It is very protective and doesn’t like Aden. Not only does Aden have to pretend he is normal and watch over his shoulder from the other delinquent foster kids he lives with, a vampire princess wants to be friends with him. Aden is oddly attracted to her but because he can see the future, he knows things will end badly if he continues to pal around with her.<br /><br />We have vampires, werewolves, talking voices and a whole slew of any other supernatural creature you can think of because Aden has some unlocked power that can summon them. What else can go wrong for Aden?<br /><br />Intertwined did not hold my interest in the least. This whole “everything and the kitchen sink plot” does not work. I think it would have been better if Gena stuck to one focus, such as Aden and his voices and try to figure out what the deal is with Mary Ann. I couldn’t help rolling my eyes when the big bad wolf suddenly appeared and began to talk to Mary Ann in her head. And don’t get me started when the Aden begins to have time traveling flashbacks.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="115355128802575487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_224511373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224511373" />
    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224511373?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=boys-i-wish-were-real">boys-i-wish-were-real</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224511373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18219357669655588233">Can I have the sequel now?? <br/><br/><b>Intertwined</b> was definitely a one-sit read! From the very beginning — when one of the four souls living inside Aden accidentally raises a cemetery — you know you're in for a totally awesome ride. The whole concept of it was original and complicated and tons of fun!<br/><br/>Plus, the originality extended to the plot which I really loved. This whole book was a breath of fresh air (with a twisting plot, an intriguing world, and lovable characters), especially that there were two s</span>
  <span id="freeText18219357669655588233" style="display:none">Can I have the sequel now?? <br /><br /><b>Intertwined</b> was definitely a one-sit read! From the very beginning — when one of the four souls living inside Aden accidentally raises a cemetery — you know you're in for a totally awesome ride. The whole concept of it was original and complicated and tons of fun!<br /><br />Plus, the originality extended to the plot which I really loved. This whole book was a breath of fresh air (with a twisting plot, an intriguing world, and lovable characters), especially that there were two sets of romances instead of one love triangle (and I can almost bet you'll guess the pairings wrong the first time around LOL).<br /><br />You know you have an awesome cast when one guy has four hilarious souls living in him (Aden), one girl is a super-sweet vampire princess (Victoria), another girl can sort of counteract Aden's ability in a way (Mary Ann), and another guy is a wicked hot werewolf bodyguard (Riley, I love you! ♥). Together they made the book even more enjoyable to read. <br /><br />Fast-paced, fun, and entertaining all the way through, <b>Intertwined</b> is a book that will have you laughing in one moment and almost crying in the next. I couldn't put it down, and I'm so excited to read the next installments in the series! <br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> If you're a lover of original paranormal fantasies, you should definitely add this to your collection! :)<br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.com/2011/10/review-intertwined.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>)</span>

  <span id="freeText7450136064640314610" style="display:none">One word. <b> Amazing. </b> Of course, I wasn't surprised, this was a book by Gena Showalter. Picking up this book I was a bit nervous because I haven't heard much about it and I don't really like books told from the perspective of a boy(there are so many exceptions to this), but I was so glad I picked up this book and started reading. I say it again. Amazing. If you loved Vampire Academy, Shadow Falls, Hex Hall and books like that, you would love this book. Intertwined takes a spin on all books full of fantasy creatures like werewolves, vampires, fairies, etc, where the main character has four souls that TALK in his head. I never read a book like this before and the fact that this was so interesting and new to me, I was instantly drawn in from the first couple of pages. I loved the characters in this book and the romance...... just amazing. Favorite character is Riley, of course but I love Aden just as much. <br /><br />You definitely need to pick up this book and read it! The story is so interesting and different and I know you will love the characters. I cannot wait to read the rest of this series, I WANT THE NEXT BOOK NOW! </span>

<div id="review_130074209" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130074209" />
    <a title="Liliana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4199142-liliana"><img alt="Liliana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533864346p2/4199142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130074209?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liliana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liliana" href="/user/show/4199142-liliana">Liliana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=ghosts-souls-spirits">ghosts-souls-spirits</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=time-traveling">time-traveling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=witches-warlocks-wizards-sorcerers">witches-warlocks-wizards-sorcerers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=supernatural-abilities">supernatural-abilities</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=paranormal-supernatural">paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4199142-liliana?shelf=faeries-fairies">faeries-fairies</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130074209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer634464075021848055">I was sooooo excited to read this book. I mean, this kid (Aden) has four souls trapped inside his head. How awesome does that sound? Well, not awesome (for him), but its certainly sounded different than any other book I've come across, which made it awesome. Plus, these four souls each have a special gift: Eve can time travel, Julian can raise the dead, Eljiah can see the future, and Caleb can posses another body.<br/>Now tell me that doesnt sound like an amazing book?<br/><br/>I started rading this book and w</span>
  <span id="freeText634464075021848055" style="display:none">I was sooooo excited to read this book. I mean, this kid (Aden) has four souls trapped inside his head. How awesome does that sound? Well, not awesome (for him), but its certainly sounded different than any other book I've come across, which made it awesome. Plus, these four souls each have a special gift: Eve can time travel, Julian can raise the dead, Eljiah can see the future, and Caleb can posses another body.<br />Now tell me that doesnt sound like an amazing book?<br /><br />I started rading this book and was totally hooked! It starts off with Aden accidentally running into a cemetary. And, of course, the dead began to rise. Then this girl (Mary Ann) walks by, and something strange happens: There's this rush of wind and Aden has to urge to go hug her and run away from her at the same time. I was like: okay this is really getting interesting now. Especially since Mary Ann can quiet the voices in Aden's head. Weird, huh?<br /><br />I thought the idea of the book was fantastic: Aden is just trying to figure out how to set these four souls free. And he wonders if Mary Ann can somehow help with that, since she can quiet the souls for some strange reason.<br />And then the vampires and werewolves showed up...<br /><br />I swear I almost face-palmed. I usually tend to stay away from vampires books. But I was like: okay, I can give this a chance, I guess. However, books like this are the reason <i>why</i> I stay away from vampire books.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Let me explain: When Aden first saw Mary Ann at the cemetary, it caused that wind and weird feelings and stuff. However, they aren't the only ones who felt this. Their energy was so strong that "mythical" creature all over the world felt it as well. And that energy drew them in. Among those creatures was a vampire princess, Victoria, and her bodyguard/werewolf, Riley. Elijah, the soul inside Aden who can see the future, saw Victoria before in a few visions. By the time Aden saw Victoria in real life, he was already half-way in love with her. Thats not the part that bothered me.<br />The part that bothered me was that Aden was willing to let Victoria drink his blood. My reaction: Are you crazy?! This is a vampire we are talking about! Sure you're in love with her, and thats totally fine, but let her drink your blood?! Are you crazy...wait, I already said that.<br /><br />In the beginning Victoria declined this...um, offer. But Elijah had already seen it happen, so it <i>would</i> happen. I felt like Aden couldn't wait for her to bite him, which was a bit disturbing for me. However, after that happened, Aden decided that he didn't want Victoria to drink blood from anyone else <i>but</i> him. My reaction: O_O<br /><br />Even more disturbing: The fact that Aden drank <i>Vicotoria's</i> blood. Sure the intention was to heal him (cuz that's what her blood does), but my reaction was still this: *cringe* *gag* *shudder* *cringe again*<br /><br />Plus, I thought vampires were supposed to be dead...er, undead (??). And by undead I mean dead, but alive, with no beating heart, of course. And with skin so cold it felt like ice, and in order to become a vampire you need to be bitten by one, AND when they walk into the sunlight they're supposed to burst into ashes. However, Victoria was the opposite of this: She had a beating heart, skin very hot, and she was actually born from her vampire mother, not bitten And the sun doesnt hurt her (this is true for only young vampires). I have to admit, the author gave a great explanation as to why this was the way it was. But still, it seemed off to me. Oh, oh, oh, one more: Aren't vampires and werewolves supposed to be like mortal enemies? And here you have Victoria, a vampire princess whose body gaurd is a werewolf... weird.<br />Come on, even Twilight got this right (well, except for the bursting into ashes part. I do like the sparkles better though, hehe).<br /><br />Okay, enough of the vampire criteria (and my Twilight rant. The Twilight part of my brain was acting up again :P). The reason why Riley and Victoria came was because Victoria's father (the vampire King whose weird name I cant remember. But he was also known as Dracula, the first vampire ever) sent them to invastigate who caused this outburst of energy. The positive thing about this, Victoria and Riley are going to protect Mary Ann and Aden from all the other creatures who want to hurt them...yay! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Another thing that bothered me about this book was the Aden-Victoria and Mary Ann-Riley relationships. They just didnt feel right. They kind of felt rushed, but thats not why I didnt like them. I usually really like the romantic relationships in whatever book I'm reading, but that wasnt the case for this one. I felt like the book would've been better <i>without</i> those relationships.<br /><br />Change of subject: Lets now talk about all the twists and unexpected turns that I happen to love in a book.<br />When Aden first met Mary Ann I thought maybe they would have something going on later. But it talked alot how they felt like they wanted to hug eachother, a sibling type of hug though. So then I started wondering, maybe they <i>are</i> related...twins even! But that wasnt the case. So now I think I'd rather much see Aden with Mary Ann instead of all these other relationships that were going on.<br /><br />Second, Since the beginning I always felt suspicious of Eve. At first I wondered if she was Aden's mother... I was so sure of it. But again, that wasnt the case. I was close though. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Turns out Eve was Mary Ann's mom! And, oh boy, does Mary Ann sure have issues involving her mom...er, moms. I didnt see <i>that</i> one coming. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />Oh and Mary Ann's wolf! There were all these hints always pointing at Shannon being the werewolf. I was like: Yeah, its him. Pffft, who wouldnt see that? Boy was I wrong yet again.<br /><br />Overall, I thought this book was pretty good. Sure I thought some things could've been left out and the plot line was totally complicated. But I liked it, not enough to say it is one of my favorites, but its still good.<br /><br />Now, the only reasons why I am going to read the next book is because I am dying to know what will happen to the rest of the souls inside Aden. And also, I want to know more about his parents. I sure hope they find them. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Oh, and did I mention that Victoria's father is no longer King of the Vampires but Aden now instead? Well he is. And I'm wondering whats going to happen, since he's human and all. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> I also want to see if the author will just try and focus on the one important thing: Aden and the souls inside of him.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://lili-lost-in-a-book.blogspot.com/2011/03/intertwined-intertwined-1.html">http://lili-lost-in-a-book.blogspot.c...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="634464075021848055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
